de la racine des dens	from the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains during extraction, it is necessary that you place moist cotton in the wound with butter for a day or two.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	As long as the joints are softened, then take hold of the pliers called "algifers", which make the patient's knee appear like a well-tended one; and do it in such a way that they resemble a file and this is its shape.
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not wish to emerge with all these claws, it is necessary that you uncover the entire flesh right up to the root, and insert the instrument which is called "althali", meaning palmache, as depicted here:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And let it be fine and thick so that it does not break at all, and if the root jumps out through this, it's good; if not, use all your instruments, as depicted hereafter:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait .ij. rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you assist with this instrument which has two points, as depicted here:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are placed according to the spacing of the teeth, and this instrument that seems like large pliers, as shown here:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	And let this tool not be able to break it, and know that few tools of bone exist; also other tools, which are not counted; and the skillful surgeons find their own instrument by themselves, according to what their operations and diseases show them. For there are parts of diseases where the old did not teach any tool because of the diversity among these and if one breaks part from the carriage or others' bones, or if it rots, then they search for the tools that suit him, which I have said, and assist with gestures, as this is their form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And may they be large and well held to hold the bone so that it doesn't escape, but can be held and removed; and then restore the place with medicines suitable for this, and if there is decay in the bone, and it's small, then find all of this instrument:
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a .i. petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the tooth appears not according to its natural form, and the shape is ugly, especially in maiden women, you should know if this tooth was born after another one and it's not in its rightful place, and one cannot pull or grind it: then extract it; and if it's next to a tooth, take this instrument that has this form, which resembles two small beaks, and is sharp from iron on the tip.
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the file slowly in my hands for the hardness of the tooth, and because you do not move the others, and if it appears that one can be filed, so I file it from half a file as it is shaped:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and similarly like the file used for making needles; and grind the tooth slowly gently in my hands for a while, until it doesn't move till it finishes; then make it flat at the end with all kinds of smoothers, if it's too sharp and it irritates the tongue, so you need to smooth out the roughness until it is even, so that it doesn't irritate the tongue nor spoil speech.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth boils
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	When the tooth in front is broken, through percussion or impact, and if the patient can't press on it that he doesn't eat until it bleeds, and you have treated them with medicines to restrict, but this works; so they must be restrained with a gold thread, for silver threads turn green and decay, but gold never changes. And use threads of less size neither too thick nor too thin, according to the size of the space between the teeth; and if you see to incline the teeth, take the thread and double it into the two healthy teeth, then place the diseased ones between the inner teeth if there is one or more, until you feel properly up to the healthy tooth on the other side; then start covering again up to where you interrupted, and pull your hand skillfully and carefully until it doesn't move; and bind your thread at the root of the tooth so that it can't escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then use thread with some pincers, and assemble them, and place them between a healthy tooth, and do so in such a way that it does not irritate the tongue; then leave it like this as tight as it can remain, if it loosens or the threads come undone, bind it again with another thread; should it stay and serve thus for all its time, and this is the shape of the teeth and the arrangement of the two healthy teeth, and the two middle ones, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	And when the tooth is dislocated, you put it back in its place gradually, just as we have said; and do not interfere with any forceful attempt which isn't cautious or endures pain, and each time one does not make the shape of a bone tooth of a cow, and then place it at the spot where the defect exists, and bind it like what we have said, and it stays and serves for as long as possible.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	covering the wound on the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	None of these threads come from under the tongue or nature, when one is born thus; or by accident in a stitched wound; and the procedures are such that you work with your mouth towards the sick area, have its head on your healthy side, and lift the tongue. Then cut this nervous thread until the tongue is dislodged from its place, and if there is stiffness or hardness, it's due to sudden trauma, then bend the hook and cut this tightly bound thread; and be careful that the incision does not go too far inward, for the artery is underneath; and when you're done, remove the rose water and coolness, or cold water, then place beneath the tongue a linen tent; and rub your fingers on the sick area each night, so the tongue cannot stick.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the bleeding starts, you should apply sulfur to the wound; and if there is no blood loss, then use a gentle heat from the cautery; this works well in such cases; then treat with other remedies until it heals.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you notice it's of color or blackish or hard, so that the patient doesn't feel anything, don't touch it because it's gangrene; and if it's turning into phlegm, and there is moisture, then cut off the hook, and make a thin incision on both sides, and relieve them from both sides; and if the nose doesn't drain in your operation area, put vinegar over the burnt spot until it's healed completely, then continue with your operation as long as you're using force; then lift the head up and wipe it with oil, and treat again until they’re healed.
des apostemes de la gorge	removal of abscesses from the throat
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	None of the glands in the throat, which are called 'godath', and properly named the two almonds. When you treat them as we have said during division, if they are not healed, then be careful: if it's hard pus-filled spots that are small and white, don't touch them with iron at all.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	And if they are red and the root is large, don't touch them with iron either, like for blood leakage; but let them bleed until it heals, then you can remove them, or they would burst on their own. And if they are white in color and have a thin root, prepare your instrument to cover them, but first check that the pus has settled and calmed down.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then have the sick person sit in front of the sun, and let his limbs be in their natural position, and let him open his mouth and hold the surgeon's fingers between his hands, and press the tongue all over with the whole instrument, as it is done; and use fine silver or thin steel just like knives.
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Can't you press the tongue with all this instrument, and you see the abscess, take the thimble and place it in the almond, then pull it down more than you can; and pull nothing from the strings with it, then cover it with the instrument until this shape forms, resembling some forces; and always let the head be bent, one after another, and are very sharp, and made of iron or silver:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument at hand, take tongs like these instead:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les .ij. amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les .ij. amandres igament.	And make the incisions on both sides and name them. When you have completed one of the glands, complete the other in the same manner, after which gargle the patient with hot, then cold water and warm water, as long as bleeding occurs, then continue to gargle with water that is hot or pomegranate seeds that are cooked, or bay leaves and similar things until all the pus has been drained. Then proceed with the treatment once it's healed. If any other abscesses develop in the throat besides the two glands, then treat them accordingly as the two glands would be treated similarly.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I treated a woman with an abscess that was inside her throat, namely the small abscess; and I had almost completely sealed off the entire throat, so that the woman could not breathe due to the blocked passage, and she could neither eat nor drink, and died if she remained like that for one or two days.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	The abscess had grown so much that it was necessary to remove two inches by the two nostrils of the nose.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I acted quickly then, and applied the antiseptic to one eye, after which I pulled it out, removing a large portion of pus. Then made another incision in the other cheek near the nose, and left her mouth open pressing down on the tongue; afterwards inserted the stick into these abscesses, and cut off some tissue, but only a little blood came out. And thus cleared the passageway to the throat for the woman, started drinking water soon after then wine, stopping from further surgery over an extended period; and the abscesses grew back immediately filling up the space I had emptied out until they were quite large; so kept working on this task within her throat cavity: she did not grow as expected; and left those areas, God alone provided for her afterwards.
de l’uve	From the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When it descends into the uterus, and it becomes swollen and long, this is called "perpendicular"; and if it's large and round, it's called "ovum".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is being treated as we have said in the division, and the treatment doesn't help, and you notice that the wound from the abscess has calmed down, and it's subtle, then it should be taken; and the one that's round and not long; and it's bloody or of a reddish color or black, then it is necessary for you to avoid making an incision on it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger for the patient.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	So when you see it, according to the way I have explained it with respect to its scent and length, you should place the patient in front of the sun, and press their tongue against the tool as we previously mentioned. Then insert an onion into the ovum, pull it outwards, and remove using the two instruments I mentioned for cutting the testicles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And it is necessary that you not remove more force than the excess which is beyond the natural limit; because if you remove more, it harms both voice and word. And after incision, use what we said about incisions of II almonds, and treat until she is healed.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient fears at the thought of surgery, it is necessary that you apply means for cautery on the sense of fear.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the method of cautery is by hot iron.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And let the patient place their head in your hand, and then press their tongue against the tool we described or the chapter on cautery, and mix with sharp live vinegar, so that it is neither too thick nor too clear; and use the force of this instrument as follows:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés .iiij. jors ou .v. Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let our head have a hair or where we put the medicine, like in movements of a spoon, and place the tool entirely with the medicine on the eye; and the patient lies still on their side so that saliva and moisture drain out of their mouth from the medicine inside, so that it doesn't go down to the throat and cause irritation; then hold your hand over all the medicine and press it onto the eye for half an hour, until you see it relieve and the medicine's actions are calmed. And if you see this, take cotton and envelop it with any tool, soak the cotton in medicine, and place the tool entirely on the cotton in sand, until the cotton dries out on the eye; and do this often, until the cauterization is complete, then let it dry, and rest for four or five days. And if you need to repeat the medicine's cauterization procedure, then repeat it, and after the cauterization, cleanse inside the eye with cotton dipped in butter, and clean off what is left of the medicine; and rinse with cold water, and rinse with gargling until it heals completely.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en .i. pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait .i. estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This treatment is safer with an incision rather than using the cautery; if it's treated by fumigation in this manner, gather lavender, thyme, oregano, rue, chamomile and parsley, and similar herbs. Combine all or some of these into a single pot, put it there, and let it boil. The pot should be well sealed with strong clay, and inside the pot place one tool according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	And whether it is made of silver or arsenic, and if one of the shoulder bones, place it in the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises to the eye via the nose as long as the eye is necrotic; after that repeat often until the eye dries out. Make sure you do not perform this at the beginning of the pus collection process, for many things can happen; and do not carry out this method when the pus starts to drain away.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this tool is not available, take a piece of charcoal and place an eggshell inside the patient's mouth so that it doesn't get too hot; because the eggshell does not let heat build up in the mouth, and together with other treatments it provides good healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou .i. morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge .i. fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren .i. estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Many times it clears the throat bone or spine of fish, without any result; if you must do this, take what you can see and press the tongue to the sun with all the instrument until you see movement. For anything that does not appear and is retracted in the throat, you should make the patient vomit so that the disease comes out as though it had been cooked in the stomach; by chance if it escapes through vomiting; or if the disease swallowed a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a crumb of dry bread; and tie to the sponge a string, then swallow her; when she comes up to the mouth, she will clear up, and then you pull with force; and if it doesn't come out through this method we've mentioned, take one tool of ash according to this shape:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	And make the tools sharp near the head so that they can enter the throat more easily and have the head raised up high; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, letting nothing pass or pushing any bone inward; ensure that the patient pushes the tool when it moves or if something is loose; if you push it down, or pull with strength equally across the entire tool until it reaches full force.
de la sansue de la gorge	of the windpipe
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	Never let the patient die from thirst, as I mentioned in division regarding treatment by medicines; and if this doesn't help, then look into the throat of the patient under the sun, and when you press their tongue against the tool I told you about.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, guide it with all care, however small each drop is, or with delicate forceps that suit this purpose.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if this does not work, take a hair comb, and use it on the patient's throat, then proceed with the movement of the comb, make sure to direct its motion smoothly, and repeat this action frequently.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if you bathe the patient in water all day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	Then take full glasses of cold water and operate the patient's mouth with it, then pour it into their throat without making them swallow immediately, and move it around with their hands often. And as soon as the water starts to be felt in their stomach, they will vomit.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if she doesn't vomit as we have said, subfuse the patient with essence of sulfur through the instrument that I mentioned for its use in eye treatment; do this many times because it will expel without causing harm.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	And the way of fumigation is this: you take the pot where there are glowing coals, and place it under a cover that has a small hole in the middle, and inside that hole should be the head of the instrument; then you pour your fumigation, and have the patient hold the tip of the stick in their mouth, seal the mouth so no smoke escapes but goes straight to the nose; and now the nostrils will begin to discharge, if it doesn't do so repeat the fumigation many times; and let the patient suffer thirst, eat salty things and others like these, and not drink water; and then they must exit through this method.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the tool with which we treat the bleeding is such that when it can be seen, it resembles curved scissors for entering into the throat; and has the appearance of a doctor's beak, and it has been sharpened like a lime, so whatever she takes in, she cannot leave; and here see this shape:
li chapistres des apostemes	The chapter on abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The appearances of pus discharges are, according to what memory brings after one and another in this book, and they are diverse in perforation and size; and it is done in two ways, where one resembles its appearance itself, and the other deals with moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	And the second way is for those who are inside the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscesses in the head are different from those in the foundation, and the abscesses in the middle of the body are different from those that come at joints, and each has its judgement in action.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced until the body is spent according to its completion; and if there are such that it must be pierced when they have grown, and do not spend according to their completion, as abscesses that are around joints.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come around joints, and it is left until they are rotten internally, by chance if the ligament and nerve of the joint have been corrupted, which causes a contraction in that limb.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	For the abscess is within the main limb, and if you delay the puncturing until it's dead, it will harm the main limb. Or it is within the base, so if you pierce or do so until it's dead; and you should not puncture an abscess without digestion having been completed, except for that which is within the base, where pus could spread fully, and be inside, and result in a fistula; and cannot heal in a large scale.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And it must be known when the time for perforating the boil that is dead according to maturation, and this is when the pain subsides, and departure of fever, and reduction in pain and heat, and movement and hardening of the head of the boil, and other signs; And you should let the perforation occur a little above the boil location or at the point where it opens, and wherever it appears. And make the perforation long throughout the body, and if the boil is on hands or feet, or joints and nerves and arteries, and all areas that do not have wrinkles.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In such cases, according to that limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in the fatty part of the body, it's good to wait until the digestion process has been fully completed before puncturing it, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before that, then the body fills with the poison of him and is full of many dirt; and by chance harden its lips and the depths of him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if there are no abscesses pierced across the width of the chest, according to what the body requires.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And it is necessary to make small incisions, small cuts; and in large abscesses, large cuts, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses where a knife should be used, and covering; when it has become as stiff as a cloth, and is softened, then one should do as with infants: And if there are those that split into three angles, and if there are those that cover like the leaf of myrtle, as abscesses from angles; and if there are those where you make a round cut, and other cuts and cutting shapes;
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Those who do not have a head, such as superficial abscesses, it must be fully punctured; and it is required when the abscess is large, and it has collected a large amount of pus, then you must puncture it, but not drain all the pus at that moment, but only a part of it. Then let the abscess subside until to another day, then leave nothing near the opening; do this repeatedly from big to small, until all the pus comes out; even if the patient has weak strength, or pregnant women, or small children, or old and decrepit people.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	For when it tries to jump every time with the issue of blood, that perhaps kills the patient, and you do not realize this.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	So avoid this chapter with great caution. When you have made your incision in the abscess, if there is an opening or wound, observe that it's size from the edge of the incision; and should be a full incision where you would use linen or cotton tents; and for large abscesses with many discharges, each must be filled with a tent so they can be placed against each other. And if you cut into the skin part in making an incision and have sutured it together internally, then it should be filled with old cotton or linseed rags without moisture until the third day; then stitch again and continue treating with ointment until it is healed properly.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if blood leaks out during your operation, cool water and easy handling should be used, and oil must cover the area repeatedly.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if bleeding persists, then apply governance and treatment, and the powders that I have mentioned in this book, and should it be in water or abscesses, and the area where the water or abscess is very nervous, you should cover the bed sheets and cloths with moistened in wine and oil; and should it be in skin, and the area is fleshy, you should cover the sheets and cloths with wetness in water and oil, or in cold wine and oil, for three days, as we have said; then remove the abscess and cleanse it, as necessary, until it heals.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And it is necessary to know this universally in treatments of abscesses: now I have told you how one should proceed before treatments of abscesses, and here comes the chapter.
des soros	of the womb
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	In the region of the head where small pus collections come about, and their methods are as in bandages, similar to a jeweler's needlework, and much is like these things.
Il en i a de gras et de telz ou il a moistor ausi com poulz; et si a de telz qui sont dur et pierous au taillier, et n’i a point de doutance se li artere n’i fait contraire.	There are some that are fatty and of such types where there is moisture too like boils; and there are others that are hard and stony to the cutter, and there's no doubt that they affect an artery without contradiction.
Et li ovraiges de la taille si est que tu esprueve a tout I estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», de coi li forme vient ci aprés, quel chose il contient.	And the procedures of cutting involve you proving with all the instrument that is called 'entromissory', from which the form comes afterwards, something it contains.
Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, do it through its entire length.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	And when the moisture has been drained, carefully scorch without leaving any residue on the skin containing that moisture, because it returns immediately if you leave nothing behind. Then dip a cotton ball in Egyptian ointment if available; otherwise, soak it in water and vinegar, then apply to the wound and let it sit until the next day; and this will cure what remains from the night.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then continue with the cotton as before, on the second day and the third, until you know well that it does not stay during the night; then apply ointment to treat the wound as suitable, while it is sound.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds in not too much fat, treat it according to this shape, along its length; and cut your incisions, and burn from all sides, and apply your entire treatment directly on the wound where it is; and if the artery goes against you, then do what I have instructed you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And also treat the abscess if it is stone-like, and cut and treat it as I have instructed you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And when cutting the stone-like abscess and moist one, it's easier as they contain less blood.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if in any of these abscesses or head or there is no moisture and from these future abscesses that I removed or head of an old woman; and found the abscess as hard as a stone, coarse and white, and could not break it; and if one had pierced none of them, one would have made the incision just like with a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	For other abscesses coming from head or ear, should these come from the infants' heads and the roots of the ears, the opening shall be left for as many days as necessary depending on its nature, so that the blood may escape; and they should be treated in accordance with what is suitable.
des scrophules	Of the scrophulae
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times these abscesses occur at the neck, and around the armpits, and under the arms, and do not come to any other part or body cavity, they are round, and they are interwoven with each other.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scab is properly within its fold, as with the nut and abscess on the head, as we have said; and the appearance of these scabs is many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to obey health measures.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In those that you see with good position in the flesh, and resemble the color of the skin, and mute from each part, not touching the neck muscles or the artery or the ducts; it's necessary for you to handle them properly above, scrape off each part of them, spread out the two lips of the mouth if needed, as we have said about abscesses on the head; then remove slowly and carefully, ensure that you do not cut through the nerve or the vein, avoid any deep cuts and scratching, keep your hands inside without going too far ahead, making sure not to cut what is unnecessary.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or artery, and this doesn't let you operate, then put vitriol broil or any powders that stop blood loss into the wound, and keep the wound restrained; leave it like this until the abscess subsides, and the wound softens, and begins to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the patient is healed, return to your work until it's completed; then follow your judgement if there are still small nodules remaining, remove and clean them.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if there is a large vein in the root of the nodule, it's not proper to remove that nodule from its root, but tie it with a double thick thread, and let it come out through it without harm; then dress the wound with old cotton dipped in Egyptian ointment, then treat it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you remove all the scabs, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound, and suture them now, then there should be no excess material due to the size of the scab.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	It is necessary that you understand how to treat its root, draw out the pus, and stitch it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scabs that contain excess matter, pierce them where they open up; and pierce them in the same manner as was said previously, dependently, then you apply poultices with ointment and similar things, so that they are corrupted by the corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then with ointment treatment applied to the flesh until it is healthy.
de squinance	regarding squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	The old ones spoke and wrote about the operation of the throat cutting; but I never saw anyone do it in our land, and this is recorded from their words.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en .ij. amandres.	For those with squinting vision, it is necessary that the incision in the throat referred to as "epiglottis" be made; and one should not seek aid for this, because all the veins and the heart are sensitive to individuals who have abscesses either inside their mouth or in the throat or between two almond-shaped structures.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the illness is within the channel of the heart, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to avoid the loss that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	Therefore, when we wish to split the epiglottis, we should split it across three circles or four small slits through them, between the two circles or by the size of the slit there, not in the cartilage; and this allows for the sectioning of the epiglottis so that no flesh remains, and the vessels are long beyond the cut.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the surgeons are fearful, it is necessary for them to stretch the throat skin across the entire inch (ounce), then cut along the keel until they reach the windpipe; and avoid the blood vessels, should you see anything, and afterwards cut the syphonic sinus, as we have said; and this is demonstrated by the section of the blood stream from the windpipe that jumps forth through the area where the body has been broken, and by the loss of voice; and leave the wound open for a piece.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les .ij. levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the time has passed since one doubts strangulation, gather the two mouths of the wound as neatly as possible, and all along the skin but not through the cartilage; then administer medicines that produce flesh until it is clean.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasim insists that one should not perform this until the throat is completely swollen, and the patient is judged dead, and the defect has been made.
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	Then cut into the epiglottis because the organs cannot move and he breathes through the wound, thus preserving him from death; and to command the old ones was to leave the wound open until the disease's malice has passed, and it has passed in three or four days. And then they commanded to sew up the wound and clean it, as long as it was cleaned; and I will tell you what I observed.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a maiden took the knife, and stuck it in her throat, and cut part of the channels from the lungs; and I was summoned to treat her, and found her as dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I uncovered the wound, and found that blood was issuing from it, and indeed she did not have a cut vein or exit route but rather her veins were exiting through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I rushed quickly and cleansed the wound so that she could be healed; and to the maiden it was only that her voice grew hoarse, and she returned after this ordeal. Therefore, I say that in tailoring the operation for removing the epiglottis, one should not fear.
de la grosse gorge	In the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	Cysts called "neck hernia" are also known as large abscesses of a deep purple color and are very common in women. They can occur in two ways: naturally or accidentally; naturally occurring ones do not involve an organ.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And accidents occur in two ways: one resembles fat that belongs to us, and the other way is like an abscess coming from our veins. There can be fear involved; thus, it's not advisable to create a surgical opening except in cases where it's small, and you thoroughly examine everything that enters: if you find something similar to our fat and unable to reach any vein, you should remove it just as one removes fat, treating its surrounding skin completely; search meticulously and treat it accordingly until it's fully healed.

et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet .ij. jors ou .iij., tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout. When the artery is damaged and the skin above it is sewn together, many times pus comes out from there. When you touch it with your fingers, you can feel it squeezing; and when it's in relation to the vein, there's an open wound appearing outward; cutting such pus is foolishness, especially when it's near the joints and angles or under the armpit or other body parts, and it's very large.

dou chancre	and gangrene
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi. de la piere	from the stone

We have discussed in the division methods for stone expulsion and medication; and we have explained the differences between mature stones that cause pain, and all their signs, as well as which stones should be surgically removed; and regarding the bladder and penis; and I will explain this clearly and briefly to you.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont .iiij. ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone in the bladder often occurs more frequently in children, and this is a sign that the urinary infection has spread throughout its subtlety; and it causes pain repeatedly, and there's a sensation of fullness in their urethra, and they urinate many times, then develop an urge again; and at these repeated urges lies the kidney; and until about four years old, children experience lighter healing due to their condition; it becomes more painful for those who are older, being somewhere between childhood and age; and the treatment is generally easier for those with larger stones than for those with smaller ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to treatment, it is necessary first to cleanse the patient by purging, in order to remove all the feces which are inside.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	Because it clogs every time when trying to cut into the stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then hold the patient by their sides, and lift them up moving downwards, so that the stone falls to the front of the bladder, and comes out no longer from its top; then have them sit between your hands, with their hands placed under their thighs, so that the bladder is fully hanging downward; then grab and touch inside; if you feel the stone in space, now hurry to cut into the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it doesn't come out completely with the toucher, wet your left hand's index finger, if the patient is young or old. Or wet your middle finger, if the patient is of adult years; and hold in his foundation, and grab the stone, and when you feel it on your finger, snip it off at the neck of the bladder; then press up to your finger, and pull out from where you see to cut.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the attendant to press the bladder with his hand, and tell him to extend his right hand up at top, and with his left hand hold the skin that is near the scrotum in the area where the cut will be made; then he pushes out the prostate gland, which is its shape:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And cut between those who are between the ribs and the foundation, not in the middle but at the edge of the left snowbank; and stand upright on the stone, and let your fingers be towards or against the foundation, and shape them like a snowball: wide outwards and narrow inside, according to the size of the stone, not too large; by chance press so much onto the finger that is against the foundation, that it jumps without effort; know that there are parts of the stone where angles and edges exist: they are sore to pierce; and if in such parts you encounter something below resembling a glistening pebble and rounded, whose exit is easy.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	And where there are angles and edges, make the size larger; if it doesn't jump, then you need to tighten with the tongs that resemble a file at their head, in order to force the stone such that it doesn't escape. Or you dig out from under the instrument using a subtle curved tool; and if you can't work this way, then widen by just a little more than half its thickness, and if it's soft on the inside, force it with vinegar; and if there are multiple stones, first break the largest at the neck of the bladder, then proceed upwards, then pull forcefully, and the smaller ones after that, assuming there are more.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	And if she is very large, then it should be removed, and make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: or he dies, or his urine starts coming out immediately after treatment when his limbs cannot heal; but nonetheless strive to drain or fragment with forceps until you remove it piece by piece. And once you have completed your task, fill the wound with frankincense and aloes and dragon's blood, bind it tightly, and place a damp cloth soaked in oil and wine, or oil and rose water and cold water, over it to cool the abscess; then set the patient up on his side, and do not untie the bandage until three days have passed.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you remove the stitches, rinse thoroughly with oil and water, then treat it with diacynicon ointment and basil ointment until it heals properly.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesses expand in the wound and cause corrosion, or blood clots remain in the bladder, and this causes urine retention in such a manner that without urination there is no escape: then you must drain your tools in the wound, remove that blood, because if it remains, it will corrode the bladder and damage it; then elevate the wound with water and vinegar and salt, and assist him in all ways possible until he recovers. And it should be that when you treat him, tie his two legs together and combine medicines over his body.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it's located where the penis leads, stuck in there, and urine can't pass; when treating as I've described, you must cut it many times, and forgive any loss due to this treatment.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have already gained this experience thus.
Pren .i. foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a .iij. angles fichiees en .i. tison:	Take one iron fork according to this form and have three pegs fixed into it:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take the thread and tie it around the penis near the stone, so that it can't come back into the bladder. Then pull out the tool in the penis gently, until you reach the stone; and push the tool into the penis slowly, until it touches the stone. And move the tool with your hand inside the stone gradually, as far as you can penetrate the stone from another side; if urine comes soon, then press your hand on the part of the stone that is still in the penis inside the passage.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it's broken in one place and jumps along with the urine, it shocks the sick. And it hurts the patient greatly; and if you can't do this for any reason that prevents you, tie a thread over the stone and another above it, then put the stick between the two threads near the stone, then pull forcefully, and release the knot, and cleanse the congealed blood in the wound; and treat until it's healed.
de la piere des femmes	From the stone of women
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por .iij. choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	It happens that stone is found within women, and if it occurs once, then it is treated carefully, and is forbidden for three reasons: one is perhaps the woman is a virgin; and the second is that no one can find out a woman who is not aware of her condition even when she is pure.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a. And the third method is that sometimes one cannot find a woman who truly understands this art of hands; and the fourth method is that the stone in a woman is often deeper than a man's stone, which means it requires a more profound incision and there is much fear involved. And if necessity calls for such action, you should seek someone well-versed in herbs, and place your hand where you find her, and if you cannot find one, then at least do not choose the shallowest option; and bring forward an experienced woman's remedy or a woman who understands part of this art and instruct her to perform what I am asking about the stone; and look very carefully whether that woman is virgin: then she must push her womb outwards, search for the stone; and when she finds it, force it back into her womb and advise her to push her womb down onto the female organ, squeeze both hands on her pelvic area firmly.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains. si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the signs to determine the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it is not bleeding, put sulfur powder on the wound for an hour until the bleeding stops. Then return to your work as long as the bone is still bleeding and have with you the tools I told you about in the extraction of stones so they can assist you in your task; and if it does not bleed and it's from a cut artery, put the powder on the wound and tie bandages and don't repeat this method again. Leave the stone and do not remove it, for fear that the patient might die by accident; then treat the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the blood has subsided and the limbs are resting, return to your work as long as the stone remains intact.

Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit .i. autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non. de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess in the breasts
