Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So do not hurry to pierce but let him die until the pain is relieved; and then place the patient on his seat, with two small seats where he can lean, supporting himself on his back and assembling his legs towards parts beneath the knee; and spread out his arms over his thighs and tie them well with a strong bandage; then guide the patient to the right side of his body, and bring the tool used for working on the marrow into place from the mouth of the patient, from which comes this form; so when you see the tool being brought into place, make sure that its position at first is to determine how deep the marrow goes, so that whatever enters through the tool does not go deeper than it should and cause injury to the patient; and if the tools are too large, cover the depth of the marrow with cloths, so that the tools do not cause discomfort; and let him place the funnel of the tool above, and sharpen the tool.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened, and one lets it drain with gentle hand, then it should be covered at the head, on the wound's edge. And when the bowel has been emptied, then it is fitting to put in the wound oiled-soaked cloths or oiled-pressed oils; place the cloths so they lie against the wound’s border and cover the margin with oiled cloths underneath a clean, moistened cloth in water or cooked vinegar; then after two days of balm application until healed, always lift out the margin and wound using an aqueous solution of honey and then of water or cooked roots of lettuce and long-leafed aristolochia; afterwards apply balm again.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is being treated with maris, then it is fitting that you avoid cooking with iron, but treat it as we have said in the section on treatment.
de l’enfantement	Of childbirth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	Proficiency is first in knowing the form of natural childbirth, and these signs are as follows: when you see a woman preparing to give birth and desiring to smell something, then the child begins to exert force to emerge. At this point, you know that the delivery proceeds according to its natural form and emerges through its head, followed by its body; and when you see these signs, it is appropriate to gently press on her belly so that the child comes out quickly. For when they descend through their head, the body follows them, and is born cleaned of its excesses via proper delivery care; anything else does not occur naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it happens at no time through its bones, and emerges from the body or the shoulder, and hands, or through its belly, or in the groin, and is converted by chance through its neck, and through other malicious shapes; it requires that a midwife be wise and subtle in these matters, and beware of error and deception, and I will show you all the shapes as to how one should assist her.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	When the child comes forth through its head by natural outlet, and the woman labors heavily in childbirth, and her strength is weak, make her sit on a stool or have women hold her; and from this nature where fenugreek has been cooked, then place the midwife between her hands with the small spoon that follows here in form:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	And cut the second [infected] part, and remove as much of the moisture that is contained inside; and press on the woman's abdomen until the child descends. If it does not descend, then one should treat the woman with fennel seed decoction mixed with safflower oil; afterwards, have her drink and inhale camphor, and hold her mouth and nose for an hour: thus the child is expelled now.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if these two hands come out far, you should gently pull them in and out; and if they can't enter, place the woman on a stool and raise her feet. Then lift off the stool from the ground, and cut the woman as she's being lifted so that she doesn't relieve herself. And if neither hand can enter and the child has died, take a knife beforehand and extract the baby, then pull equally.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	From the birth of the child from its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child is coming from its feet, what should be done is to push it up high; and then turn it little by little, until it becomes equal; then take hold of the feet and spread them little by little.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can't he jump up to his hips, if the command is given, and makes him snort with consideration; if it jumps further, may God will it.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it doesn't change like what we have said, if you turn it a little bit at a time, as long as it follows the natural shape.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	Therefore, handle it lightly.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	And if it doesn't jump as we have done, say take a muscillaige of high altitude, and oil of sesame, and gum that has been melted, and grind all in the mortar; and place this ointment inside and outside the woman's nature, then make her sit in warm water until under the ribs; and when she is moistened thoroughly, have her wear a mirrre collar, and put it on her, and leave it on for an hour; then make her sit on a stool, then make her snort and restrain her mouth and nose, and touch her belly lightly, because the child is jumping now.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	From the birth of the child upwards to his knees
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse. de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	from the birth that occurs when a hand comes out during delivery.
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer. It's necessary that the barber clean his hand, then turn it gradually and gradually, and gently apply it. de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	In the same manner for all the second half
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement. de l’issue des gemelz	from the passage of the twins
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent .iij. ou .iiij.; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	You know that twins are born often, and sometimes three or four at a time; and this is not an unusual thing, it just happens.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two things are extracted and do not live, if you ask; I know this, that they multiply and are exposed by the syphilitic affection which devises them, which is bound to the blood; and none of them emerge naturally as all under one, just like we have said.

de plusors enfans	of multiple children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	None of them are formed in the Maris I through XV or more than this, and they are all shaped like children by the measurement of their glorious humor, and it is necessary that the fluid know all this, for such a thing might happen; do so according to what is fitting.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; if insert the nail in its eyes or neck or mouth or palate or under beard or collarbone or near ribs, and if the descent happens by feet, it's inserted or a knife is used at midcosts; it's proper to trim the nail with his right hand, put the handle between his left fingers, and grease it lightly on all sides, and insert the nail in none of these areas that we've mentioned until he reaches the empty place; this is the shape of the nail:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	Then find another bone, or the third one if you must, so that the extractions are equal; and then move them equally from side to side, so as to facilitate extraction, and ensure that the bones have teeth for gripping when needed, as this is how it should be done.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if any part remains, if it has lost some of its senses from that place, and bind it in this part, and remove the other part; and if no part remains, then place this bone or higher up, do as follows until everything comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be pulled back due to squeezing, then you should cover it with a cloth until it completely comes out; then cut in the joint of the sole or at the cut line, and similarly do this for the other hand, and for both feet.

And if the child's head is large and it is entangled in the exit, or if it has an assembled sharp point, then you should push the thorned spatula between your fingers, and place the point and extract the sharp; or pull it with the tool called 'almidach', from which its form comes along with the tools or chapter that follows this one; and thus do the same for children with large heads naturally; and then pull the bones with force using tweezers, and if the head jumps out quickly and stays in strength, while the moisture is inside; and if it cannot exit, remove pieces of it as you can; and if it is swollen in the belly or under the ribs, then puncture until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if the swelling is on his feet, it causes light pain, and the flow towards the mouth of the vein is light.

And if it is entangled in the belly or udder, then you should extract by pulling out the skin roll covering it on the hand; and pull the belly or the udder as far as the moisture is exiting. And if any other member is osteitis (inflammation of bone), and the child remains, then force your thumb in from the backside of the cow's mouth, and pull until you reach the mouth of the teat; then force out the quarter or halves, and pull with strength; and if the mouth of the teat is narrowed by a clot that has come up, it doesn't suit to try and push; rather, it suits to administer things moist and greasy; and apply ointments there, and soak in a liquid softener and moisturizer.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if the child is on his side, and you can put him level, then follow what we have said about the live birth infant; and if it cannot be done, then take the fetus apart piece by piece, leaving nothing of the second stage.

And when you have done this, follow what we have said about the treatment of pus-filled blisters that come in marriage; and if there is a discharge of blood, then it should be treated with water, restraining it, and apply other treatments.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut .i. autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whom there had been an abortion of a fetus, then examined another on that spot, and found it also to be abortive.

je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was summoned for the treatment, and I thought for a long time, and couldn't find a way to heal the wound.

Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I was very surprised because the belly should not have any bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	If I thought they were bones from a dead child.

I examined the wound, and in my hands until the woman was at her best condition; and kept the woman long in this state, and it became a bit of blood from below. And I recall having written this chapter only because when the masters find an unusual thing, they should know how to provide assistance.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	To return the arm to its place
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a .ij. tornans as .ij. chiés des .ij. liiens.	Following is the form of the presser, which the books refer to; and in two turns for each shoulder at four joints.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	Always, the horns should be more delicate than the restrictor and made of wood or boxwood. And the mouth should be twice as wide as the trunk at its base, and the branches must be long one palm and a half; and in between the two trunks there should be two joints of this same trunk, which are firm on each side, about half a palm from front to back or slightly more. And these two joints are set into the mouth of the vice so as to open when you turn the two horns.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Another form, resembling more delicacy and lightness, should be made of a boxwood or ebony trunk according to the shape of the pliers; and it must have two horns at its base. As you see here, they are each one palm long and about eight inches wide; and when you observe the vice fully open with all the instrument, place the woman on her bed, her legs hanging down and her legs spread apart, then position both joints together in the vice, holding the head of the tool between her thighs. Then work your hand over the whole instrument just as you would do with the pliers similarly, according to how you see the mouth of the vice open, until she gives birth as she wishes it.

des plaies	from injuries
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have discussed the treatment of wounds in the previous section; now we will discuss hand care and medicine according to their completion.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I state that wounds are various depending on how they were caused, and where they were inflicted, as well as the reason for their occurrence.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The reasons for injuries are due to blows from stones, the size of a sword and a knife, or from spears, sticks, or arrows, or other similar things; or according to the nature of the body, such as a wound on the neck, or on the head, or on the chest, or on the abdomen, or on the liver, and similar parts; and I will tell you how to treat each wound, starting with simple injuries to the head, because the memory will come in its chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound comes or bone injury occurs and the bone is not broken, you must be cautious to ascertain if it's due to stone or similar issues, and the skin has completely been torn open and the wound is large, and you slightly doubt for pus formation: If such is the case, take immediate sanguination of the cephalic area itself even if there is a little blood from the wound. And treat accordingly depending on the part that's removed; let the patient drink full of wine and eat heavy meat and provisions afterwards.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez. Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure. And the way to prepare the powder is as follows: take one part of incense; two parts of dragon's blood; three parts of living charcoal, and finely ground it, then apply this mixture to the wound, compacting it so that the air can circulate well and adhere thoroughly to all its blood; then tie it firmly in place, leaving it undisturbed until it doesn't swell; because medicine should not be removed while it's still healing.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And this is done only once with charcoal alone, when one does not have the incense or the blood of a dragon, but that the surgeon has cleansed the wound.

de la plaie dou col	from the wound on the neck

de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	from the wound of a spear or a knife
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it's from a spear or knife and the wound is deep, observe if the air flows out of the wound without any patient resistance: this means that the injury is fatal. And if it isn't too deep and there's fresh blood throughout, don't apply powder or bind it right away at first hour, because the blood won't clot properly due to moisture escaping and re-entering the body, making the patient ill; instead put a curative ointment on it and bind it twice a day. dou derrompement dou ventre	Regarding the protrusion of the belly
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The operations of the abdomen are large, medium, and small. A large wound can involve any part of the intestine or the intestines themselves, allowing foreign objects to enter; stitches on this require more difficulty, and it's never worse than a small wound compared to a large one, because you need to reposition the intestines multiple times when treating them, unless they're brought back in layers. This is due to the fact that the intestines swell upon contact with cold water, hence returning them further down becomes difficult. Therefore, operations of lesser wounds are better, as you can more easily maneuver and return the intestine to its correct position than with others. Be aware that there are four ways a belly wound can occur: The common stitch procedures happen in the abdominal stitch area, while stitches for other body parts and certain specific wounds follow these same common methods; however, all of them are better when dealing with the abdomen-related wounds, and I'll explain each one separately.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	I state that when the wound is small and there's no matter from the intestines involved, and if there are any injuries they need to be treated, this can be done through one of two methods: either because of the size of the wound as we have said, or due to the intestines being swollen by cold.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	And when it is cold, warm him in this manner: soak a sponge or use part of the linen garment in water alone, or you can boil it with water and add thyme and quince pith and spice, and pull on the intestines until the swelling goes away; and every time do this until the drink starts to reduce swelling.
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling depart, moisten the intestines with water or tea that has been cooked and let it cool, for by this means does the entrance allow for little matter; and if it cannot enter, then make a small cut in the wound using the instrument from which we remove gallstones; and the first treatment should be to ensure it can pass without needing any unnecessary cuts; and these are the instruments for splitting: if you cut inside along its curve and outwardly not, and observe this form.
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestinal organ jumps out, if you can place it back according to its natural form in its proper location, because this is better than leaving it out.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	When the wound is broad, and it's in the belly area, you should help the patient by lifting their back, and put their legs higher than their head. And if it's in the belly area, place the head and the buttocks higher than the belly parts, similarly when the stomach rupture is in one of the two parts, then adjust your approach so that the retracted part is above the other; and thus you should manage what I say in regards to large and medium wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds use whatever is available to you, and always have the necessary instruments at hand that will help you pierce the entire wound with the needle on both sides, then stitch it together. This is the common method of suturing, and when you need needles, take one or more depending on the size of the wound. Leave an inch from the edge of the wound before starting to sew; then insert a needle at the very beginning where there should be good strong thread; pierce both sides of the skin with the needle that is inside the skin, as much as you can into the wounded part, and join the ends of the gutters together for three stitches. Then sew through the threads twice on one side and stitch together the edges of the wound in this manner until all the wound is joined; use needles of moderate size between fine and large, because sharp needles cut through the flesh completely, while very thick ones do not enter well. These should be medium-sized needles; avoid sewing too far out from the flesh and skin so they don't tear open before suturing starts; then tie off each stitch when you're done so they won't irritate the patient at night. Cover the needle holes with bandages or cloths to prevent irritation, and leave them in place until the wound has healed; this method of suture works best for small wounds as it requires only one needle for every second stitch and joining both gutters together on one needle with strong medium thread; after piercing all four ends together, pull back the needle from where you started sewing like when you weave cloth. Leave an inch between each stitch as large as a thumb's width; this kind of stitching heals patients well, and I sewed up a belly wound that had been cut by a knife, which was nearly a palm wide, contained several palms' worth of intestines and was in the middle of the abdomen.
Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I brought back the intestine then after it had been out for twenty-four hours, and the wound healed up to fifteen days, and I treated him, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And when the doctors had judged that he would die, it was a miracle; and I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where none could be found or any medicine; instead, I changed a piece of old cotton twice a day on his wound and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing: take the needle and insert it from below up until it reaches inside; when it has pierced through the skin straight up and down, then place your thumb on the suture or wound location where you have inserted the needle, and let the needle pierce through again from inside to outside at another part; and with this type of sewing, you sew in the same manner as the squirrel furs their fur, leaving a hole once on one side and pick it up again on the other, until the entire seam is completed.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune.	The second method of sewing, as Galen properly described it, is such that no one does, who combines the two natural parts together, and applies one end of a needle or thread to another end, in this manner: put one needle or thread close to a piece from near the edge, then make only one opening on this side and leave both pieces from the edge; then turn the needle, and have it pierce from below just inside up to where the two pieces from the edge are; then pierce through both of them from below just inside with two other threads or needles that come from the opposite side; and this is the method of sewing and the most common.
Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galen said this word, and no one affirms it, that the belly should be stitched with two needles or each thread; and one needle must be inserted on one side of the wound, and the other on the opposite side, as those who stitch corroies do. Know that when the injury is in the middle of the belly, this stitching is more grievous than others' work on their bellies.
Li jugemens de la plaie si est telz com li jugemens des autres plaies: et est que quant tu trueves la plaie fresche a tout son sanc, ainsois que li ars l’ait muee, si remet arer l’intestine, et lou cout; puis met sus la poudre enjanrant char, et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucun oignement que soit present, tant que li plaie bowe; et chicent li fil, et soient soudez li sifac, et li mirach; puis cure la plaie si com les autres, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu n’as medicines, si met sus, tantost qu’ele comance a giter bowe, coton viel, et le remue II fois le jor tant k’il soit sanez.	The judgments of the wound are similar to those of other wounds: and this is that when you find the fresh wound completely filled with blood, as long as the art has done its part, you should reinsert the intestine, and the mouth; then apply some stimulating powder on the char. And if the art has performed its task, place no ointment until it heals; while the wound heals; then sew up any lacerations, and seal the sifac and mirach. Then treat the wound as you would others, until it is healed; and should you lack medicines, apply an old cotton cloth at the start, changing it twice a day until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis.	For you do not need other medicine in various conditions when the wounds are simple; and if you fear that the wound might spread to the main members, then it is necessary for you to soak feather linen in oil heated with heat, or in rosmary oil, and place it between joints, and around the elbows; and if there's pain or gangrene anywhere, and this happens many times, then you should clear out black wine as a cathartic, and similarly, if gangrene reaches to the intestine; and puncture inside it. And know that when it is large intestines, it heals more easily than small ones.
Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	The intestine known as 'young' cannot heal when it is diseased, and this is due to the obstruction of veins that reside within, and the subtlety of the entire body, along with its proximity to nerves in terms of its nature.
Et si li zirbe saut de la plaie, si le remet arrier ausi com l’intestine, tandis qu’il est fres; et s’il est vielz et devenus vers ou noir, si covient que tu lies le leu qui est noir, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, car il i a voinnes et arteres; puis cope ceu qui est entre le liien, et met les II chiés pendans des la partie desoz la plaie jusque defuer por aligier l’estraction quant li zirbes chiet, et li plaie bowe.	And if the knot jumps out of the wound, then place it back again as with the intestine when fresh. And if it is old and turned towards or black in color, it's necessary that you tie up what is black, so no bleeding occurs from it, for there are veins and arteries inside. Then cut open the link, and hang the two ends on either side of the wound until out past its edge, to ease extraction when the knots fall off, and let the wound heal over.
de la routure dou boueil	from the rupture of the bladder
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, it can sometimes be restored in some forms, as I have seen that a man was wounded by lance or stomach; and the wound was on the right side of the stomach, it got infected and became a fistula, with the discharge and wind. I treated it according to what seemed right to me, and continued refining until it healed, and sealed up the wounds.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	And when I saw him bound, I doubted that the patient might have pain in his belly; and there was no harm but he stayed in better conditions, eating and drinking; and said none of the experimentors that if he had a small wound in the intestine, it must be tied in such manner: take furs with large heads, then join the edges of the wound together, and when the fur has opened its mouth, place it over the two lips, if it tightens its mouth upwards; and then press down on its head, and this should stay so that it cannot slip out, then put another fur in this way after before, until the whole wound is covered; and thus the wound heals.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.	If a foreign body lodges in the intestine and causes no harm to the patient, one can tie the intestine with a thin thread cut from the intestine of an animal, like this: take most of the intestines out from this thread's end, then attach it onto the main part of this thread. Then insert the thread into the needle, sew the intestine and stitch it back together; do so in such way that the stitches resemble the weave of a fabric or hope. And when the wound is large and wide, especially if it's located within one of the large intestines, it must be treated carefully to ensure no infection occurs due to its complexity.
de fistule ou qu’ele soit	from a fistula, or if it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	Know that any wound or abscess, when it matures, is universally called 'fistula', even if it's hair-covered and swollen.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And fistula is according to the true swelling firm and white, or one where you don't feel pain, and it's also covered like feathers of a bird; and sometimes it's clear in size, and at other times it's thick; sometimes small, and at other times quite large; and I have spoken about this under the division of wounds, that any wound not healed, and if there is no flesh present, leaves through one of the eight causes: namely, due to the tiny quantity of blood or pus; or because of its malice; or because there's hard flesh inside, and on the skin, which doesn't allow for pus to form; or there's too much pus; or the lungs are damaged, and the matter has a bad quality; or the medicine used in treatment isn't good; or because of how putrefaction occurs in pestilence-like manner; or due to its nature's slow digestion process, which also slows down healing, and is expelled by itself; or there's veins or bones present. And I have already shown all these causes, their signs, and the uses of medicines under this division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	So it is necessary for me to inform you about the treatment of fistulas which is performed through manual work.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Know that fistulas exist in all body members; for there are fistulas that originate from large veins, and arteries, and nerves, either internally or externally, or within the stomach, bladder, lungs, or any of the ribs, or the spinal column, or any joint of hands or feet; and when this affects the main function of a limb, in which they appear.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the fistulas that occur in this manner are due to negligence and lack of knowledge. There is no other explanation than digging or misunderstanding; if there is any fistula that does not extend until what I've mentioned, then you have made a treatment mistake, and you realize its location, so take spider silk or iron wool; if the fistula is straight, use it; and if the fistula is curved, use a subtle silver tool to search for its way since silver bends with the curve; and if the fistula has lost its path and you cannot properly search through tools, then flush it by one of those paths because moisture flows from one path to another, clean it out. Then wisely cut it according to your strength, find out whether there is bone or nerve passing through it fully, and ask the patient about the pain they feel when pressed with your hand, and where they feel it; and when you truly know its location and that it's far from joints, nerves, arteries, veins, or any of the parts I've mentioned, treat it according to what I've said, remove the pus and rotten matter inside it; then continue the treatment until it is healed. If the fistula has been properly cut at a right angle, then it is fitting that you cut into its full length as much as possible, then put wet bandages soaked in an ointment into the medicine water, and replace them up to the mouth of the fistula, until the medicine can corrode the excess left inside; and then apply healing dressings until it heals completely. If it has not healed by this method, cauterize it as we have said, and if the bone is rotten due to the fistula, then cut into it.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If the vein or nerves are not hindered or main limbs, as we have said; and if the bone is exposed, and there's decay and darkness, you must remove the king until all decay is gone, then treat with hot substances until it becomes healthy; and if it doesn't become healthy and returns to its original state like before, know that you are not finished up to this point: so uncover and clean until you're at the bottom, and remove all the decay, then restore the place; and if it is in such a state of health afterwards, then it's well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption has spread too far, and you cannot restore it. If there's no other option than to leave it to nature; and if there is only a small corrupted bone, and you can pull it with your tweezers, use an appropriate tool for this task, and if there are many bones, remove all of them but don't leave any behind; and if moisture is making things difficult, without error or fear, combine force, moisture, and heat, and free the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you can't remove them within an hour, place something stimulative for putrefaction on the wound and leave it until the flesh has rotted inside the bones completely. Then they will become lighter in weight; and if it is a large bone such as from a leg or thigh, remove it up to where all of the corruption has been taken out, then heal the wound; and if there's a significant part of the putrefaction that reaches down to the bone; you should treat everything until it reaches the putrefaction, and then continue healing until it is sewn together; and I will tell you about an ailment which occurred in someone's leg where you would take it as an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	There was once a young person around thirty years old, who had pain in their leg due to something that came from within the body, until the substances reached the leg, and there was an inflamed lump (abscess), and no reason could be found to open it; but the doctors by their folly opened so much that the abscesses were opened, and they ate away at a lot of tissues, and became a fistula, and they suffered many losses that caused the entire body to be swollen and full of pus; and many doctors continued this treatment for two years, and there was no wise man in the art of medicine until I was called, and saw their leg and the medicines used on it, and what was eaten away by the pus within the body; and the parts of the body that were affected became red like youth's skin, and had a yellowish color.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent at one of these hollows, and then searched all the hollows, finding that some came against each other from all parts of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I hurriedly acted, and cut into one of the hollows until I discovered part of the bone, finding it decayed and pierced through; I saw that the corruption extended all the way to the innermost parts of the bone; it appeared as though it was the decay that stood out from the bone, so I thought there was no other corruption than what I had uncovered; I began to heal the wound with medicines for a long time, but could not stitch it together; then I started again and found the bone just as before, discovering that the corruption continued within the bone. Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	For during blood evacuation, it often happens, but it was completely healed. In the place of the bone came out a hard flesh, and it had good disposition and did not cause any harm or opposite anywhere at all, neither in appearance nor in function.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	And if the bone is broken in any part of the body, as it should be done: take hold and pull at the end of the bone that sticks out, and command it to extend upwards; and put another rope made of thicker wool than the first one, and tie it on the flesh coming out from inside the bone, pull up the top so that you remove the rotten flesh underneath, reveal the new flesh where there was a break, ensuring not to harm the new flesh; place coal or a board under the bone to replace the rotten flesh. You should do this as much as visible and felt decay allows, and repeat this process again if necessary.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the bone is rotten and does not open up, or if the corruption is within or in a part of it, then uncover all the flesh; then place the tip over it, and thereafter allow the infection from one part to the other until you cover it for as long as the infection lasts, just like we said; and if the corruption is inside a joint, remove the corrupted joint and place bone on the opposite side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, there must be another angle than that which needs to be cut through; and if the corruption lies under a finger of your hand or foot, it's very hard work indeed, but still you must investigate this corrosion according to how it opens up; and clean it with all means possible yet so that neither the vein nor nerve prevent you from doing so; know that both the incisioner and tool are for cutting these bones in various manners depending on the bone structure, appearance of its edges, size, fineness, size, thickness and hardness; thus each work must show which tool suits its needs according to knowledge of this art form and the testimony about illness modes. dou feu	by fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	The joints become dislocated either through internal causes or external ones; and when you have treated this corrosion via the medicine cure, but it doesn't improve, then one must treat that member until where the corrosion occurs, so that the patient escapes from death or from the harm caused by the deficiency of the body; and the signs are: the limbs turn black, as if they were burned by fire, and after the blackness comes that corrosion spreading member by member, and it takes over the whole body; you should hurry to treat this corruption, and if it's due to the impact of some poisonous animals such as sea scorpions and snakes, and alike, when the corrosion affects the head of the body, then treat it, and don't give it space to reach up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it reaches up to the hand, if you fix the joint, so that the corrosion doesn't extend up to the elbow; and if it extends to the elbow, if you take care of the wrist; and if it passes the wrist, it's death, and nothing can be saved beyond its quantity of power; and in this way, when the corrosion comes or progresses: If it comes at the first joint, if you fix after the other joint; and if it progresses or spreads at any point, if you treat all that point; and if it ascends into the leg, if you treat at the joint of the knee; and if it reaches above the knee, there is no other option than to let the patient die from the loss; and the method for treating or keeping the limb involves binding it up both over and under, spreading one gauze across each layer of bandage, and placing another gauze on the other side moving upwards, and you cut out the flesh between the two layers until the bone is exposed; then treat or care, and place a piece of linen from each side, so that the care does not touch the healthy part, and brings no further injury or pus to the patient.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	And if blood comes out when you operate, if you quickly cauterize it or put on some restricting powders; then return to your medicine until its completion, then bind the limb with a suitable bandage and treat until it heals. And I will tell you what happened to this man: he had a blackness that seemed like a flame burn and the corrosion came first in his right foot, until she consumed all of his flesh; and when the man saw the corrosion, he rushed to cover his foot, and became well.
