It can be felt starting from part to part until it reaches the skin where it goes, and it jumps around; it's infected with the corruption of various fluids, such as worms, snakes, maggots, or roundworms in the stomach; one wonders about its maliciousness because when it travels through the body, and it ascends to the head, and comes to the eye by chance, it can return, and destroy the eye; this happens many times.
Quant tu le vues curer et traire, si ne puet on fuers que quant il vait: si covient donques que tu lies le leu desus et desoz d’un fort liien bien estroitement, puis cope sus et le trai fuer, et se li vers est em parfont en la char, et tu ne le trueves, si le cauterize de feu sus, tant qu’il muire; et li plus grans nuisemens que il fait, si est qu’il corront l’oil, si com nos avons dit; et se tu le vois venir ou chief pres de l’oil, si estraint desoz lui le sorcil forment, puis cope sus, et le trai fuer; et covient user le malaide de mundifiement de cors de medicines solutives por les males humors porries, et se warse de viandes enjanrans porriture.	When you see it being treated and drained, one can only do so as follows: therefore, it is necessary that when it goes: thus, it must be that you tie the head above and below with a strong tightly bound rope, then operate upwards and drain it, and ensure it moves fully in the flesh, if you don't find it, then cauterize it with fire until it heals; and among its greatest injuries, these are when they affect the eye, as we have said; and should you see it coming near to the eye, then firmly restrain below him the eyebrow formed, then operate upwards, and drain it; and must use the aid of purification of bodily fluids from medicines that dissolve substances for illnesses due to body miasmas, and be wary of eating rancid meats that cause putrefaction.
de la dolor qui vient de ventositeit	The pain comes from wind disturbance
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «vakirir», et est une dolor que vient en aucuns membres, et pues se mue de membre en membre; et je vis ceu que je vos di.	This illness is called in our land " vakirir ", and it's a pain that occurs in any limbs, and spreads from limb to limb; and I've seen the things I'm telling you.
Je fui apelez a une femme malaide, et me descovrit som bras, et vis une petite enfleure en la voinne dou brais; et I poc aprés, li vis monter ausi com un ver a l’espaule, plus tost que nulle chose, ausi com vif argent quant il cort de leu a autre; li dolor se departit de celui leu, et se ficha en l’espaule, et puis un poc aprés corrut par tout le cors, tant qu’ele vint en l’autre brais; puis me contait qu’elle tornioit adés entor le cors, si com je la vis.	I was summoned to attend a sick woman, and I examined her arms, and saw a small swelling in the vein near her arm; shortly after, I noticed it growing as fast as a worm on her shoulder, quicker than any other thing, like freshly cut silver when taken from one place to another; the pain left that spot, and settled into her shoulder, and then a little while later spread throughout her entire body, until it reached the other arm; she then told me that it had returned within her body, just as I had seen.
Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I was amazed at how she moved member by member in such a way, for I had never seen this illness done in this manner.
Toutevoie, je avoie veut maint que bien avoient veut movoir dolor de leu a autre, mais je ne l’avoie mie veut, si com je le vis en la femme; et je me pensai que c’estoit por ceu que li femme avoit sec cors, et les voinnes descovertes, et por ceu apparoit celle ventositez constrainte; et n’aperent mie selonc ceste raison a ces qui sont delicious, et qui ont moistes cors et voinnes reponues.	In short, I have wanted many times that the pain in one place move to another, but I did not want it myself, as I saw with the woman; and I thought it was due to the woman having a dry body, and her veins exposed, and because of this, that constrained windiness becomes visible; and they do not understand according to this reason those who are delicious, and have moist bodies and their veins covered.
Et quant tu vues curer ceste maladie, et li malaides sent celle dolor, s’elle t’apert si com nos avons dit, si la lie desus et desoz hastanment, et puis cope sus tant que cele ventositez constrainte au leu isse fuer; et cauterize le leu; et se tu ne la vois a tes eulz, si le cure de ceu qui deboute les ventositez, si com pilules fetides, et pilules de serapin, et semblans autres.	And when you see it treated for this sickness, and the patient feels that pain, if it opens up as we have said, apply pressure above and below rapidly, then continue applying pressure until that wind force escaping from the body; cauterize the body; and if you don't see it at your eyes, treat the one who debouches the winds, such as rotten pills, pill of serapin, and similar others.
des saiettes	arrows
Les saiettes sont diverses, selonc lor semblances et selonc les leus dou cors ou elles chient.	The arrows are various, according to their appearance and according to the nature of the animal they come from.
Li diversitez de lor si est qu’il i a de celles qui ont grans pointes, et petites, et chevees, et soudees; et de celles qui ont II angles, et de celz qui ont lengues, et de celles ou il a pieces; et celle qui chiet en aucun membre si chiet selonc II manieres: ou en membre principeil cheveit, si com cerveil, cuer, foie, pormon, rains, intestine, vessie, et semblans membres.	The diversity of them lies in the fact that there are arrows with large points, small ones, barbed, and soldered; and those with two angles, as well as those with tongues, and those made up of pieces. And among them, some discharge without affecting any member, while others do so according to two ways: or they pierce a principal member such as the head, brain, heart, liver, stomach, kidneys, intestines, bladder, and other similar parts.
Quant elle chiet donques en aucun leu de ces membres, et li signe de mort, que je te dirai ci aprés, t’aperent: si covient que tu te warses de l’estraction de ceste saiette, car li mors vient aprés en plusors dispositions; et quant cist mal signe ne t’aperent mie, et li saiette n’est mie em parfont, si la trai, et cure la plaie.	When it hurts therefore in no part of these limbs, and the sign of death, which I will tell you later, appears: so you should be ready for the extraction of this arrow because death follows in multiple conditions; and when that bad sign is not seen and the arrow is not fully extracted, then pull it out, and treat the wound.
Et li signe dou cerveil quant li saiette i chiet et perce l’os, et saut li syfac fuer qui est sus le cerveil, est quant scotomie et sode et esvertin et roujor ens eulz, et enflammation et roujor de lengue, et spasme et permixtion d’entendement, et vomissemens de cole; et per aventure ist sans fuer des narines, ou des oreilles; et par aventure pert la parole et la voix; et saut de la plaie moistor blanche semblant a poulz, et en saut ausi com bruee de char; et se cist signe t’aperent, si te tien de la cure, et trai la saiette s’elle n’est ens.	And the sign of the brain when the arrow hits and pierces the bone, and jumps the spinal fluid which is above the brain, is when paralysis and numbness and inversion and redness of the eyes, and inflammation and redness of the tongue, and spasms and confusion in understanding, and vomiting of bile; and sometimes lacks strength from the nostrils, or the ears; and sometimes loses speech and voice; and there's a white moisture at the wound that looks like pus, and also burns similarly to burned flesh; and if this sign is seen, take it seriously and extract the arrow if it isn't yet.
Li signe de la siette quant elle chiet ou cuer, sont qu’elle est pres de la mamele senestre, et sent ausi com s’elle estoit fichie en chose dure, ne mie vuide; et par aventure li siette se muet ausi com li poulz, et en cort noir sanc, et vient froidor et suor froide, et sincope: saiches adonc sens doute ke li mors dessent.	The sign when the heart or seed drops is that it's near the left mammary gland and feels as if it were inserted into something hard, not empty; and by chance the heart also stops like a pulse, and black blood comes out, and brings on coldness and cold sweat, and fainting: therefore know without doubt that death is approaching.
Et li signe de la saiette que nevre lou pormon est que sans plains d’escume saut de la plaie, et li gorge enfle, et li malaides mue color, et sospire haut et quiert le froit ar.	And the sign of the arrow that doesn't leave the body is that it bubbles up from the wound without much foam, and the throat swells, and the patient's face changes color, and they sigh loudly with their breath.
Et se li saiette chiet en la coverture dou pis, si est delez les petites costes; et giete grant alainne et grant dolor et sospire; et li muevent tuit li membre des espaules.	And if an arrow stops within the buttock's covering, it penetrates below the small ribs; and causes great pain and much agony, along with sighing; and all parts of the body from the shoulders move.
Et se li saiette chiet ou stomac, par aventure si saut de la plaie aucune chose de la viande indigeste.	And if an arrow stops in or near the stomach, by chance it may spill any undigested meat from the wound.
Et se li saiette chiet ou ventre, et en saut point de fien par l’intestine rout, si n’a point d’esperance en la cure, ne en l’estraction de la saiette.	And if an arrow stops in or near the belly, and it does not pass through the intestines on impact, there is no hope for treatment, nor in removing the arrow.
Et se li saiette chiet en la vessie, et li urine en saut et vient defuer, et li malaides sent fort dolor: saiches que li plaie est mortelz.	And if an arrow stops inside the bladder, and the urine flow is interrupted and spills out, causing great pain to the patient; know that this wound is fatal.
Li autre membre, si com li faice et li colz et li gorge et li espaule et li adjutoire et li espinee dou dos et li forcele et li cuixe et les jambes, et li membre semblant, sont sauf selonc plusors dispositions.	The other limbs, such as the arms and shoulders and neck and spine and ribs and hip and pelvis, and all similar limbs, are safe according to various positions.
Quant li saiette est en lou nerf ou l’artere, et elle n’est venimouse, si com je vos dirai qu’il m’avint, por ceu que vos faciez autretel.	When the arrow is in the nerve or artery, and it's not poisonous, as I will tell you what happened to me, because you did something else.
Il avint a I home c’une saiette li chut ou larmier en la racine dou neis: je la tentai, et la traï d’autre part desoz la graisse de l’oreille, et fut sanez sens nusement.	It happened to one of the people when an arrow hit him below the nose at the base of his ear: I tried it and moved it from another side through the fat of the ear, and found no serious injury.
Et traï a un jeu une saiette que li chut en la graisse de l’oil desoz la papiere desoz, et li saiette estoit reponue, et n’en poi ataindre que la pointe devers lou fust, et estoit li saiette grans d’un arc turcois, a tout I fer legier sens oreilles; li jeus fut sanez, et ne li vint nulz mavais accidens.	And tried out an arrow that had hit him in the fat near his eye under the paper, and the arrow was found to be intact, unable to reach anything but the tip towards the shaft, and was a large arrow like a Turkish bow's length, without any damage to the person who performed it; the game was fine, and no bad accidents occurred.
Et traï une saiette de la gorge a un crestien, et estoit li saiette arabique a oreilles: je soiai les barbions, et subtiliai tant que je la traï, et fut sanez li crestiens.	And take an arrow from the throat to a Christian, and this was the Arabic arrow with ears: I would shave off the stubble, and trimmed it finely as I pulled it, resulting in the death of the Christian.
Et traï une saiette a I home, que li estoit cheue ou ventre, et pensai qu’il moroit; et puis qu’il ot passez XXX jors, si ne mua point sa disposition; je taillai sus la saiette, et l’engignai, et la traï fuer, et n’ot point de mavais accident.	And pull an arrow from I house, that was stuck in the back or belly, and thought he was dying; and then after thirty days, if it didn't change its position; I cut into the arrow, I sharpened it, and pulled it out, and there was no bad accident.
Et si vis I home cui une saiette chut ou dos, et fut li plaie soudee sus; et demora li saiette dedens li, et ne chainja point ses dispositions naturez, ne ne trova nuisement en aucune de ses oevres naturelz.	And if an arrow falls or pierces the back of a house, and the wound is joined from within; and the arrow stays inside, and doesn't change its natural positions, nor does it find harm in any of its natural works.
Et vis I autre homme, cui il chut une saiette en sa faice, et fut soudee li plaie; et demora ensi sens soffrir grant dolor; et mout d’autres semblans.	And see another man, who was hit by an arrow in his face, and had the wound stitched up; and suffered great pain thereafter; and many others like this.
Et traï une saiette a I home des princes le roi, que li estoit cheue enmi lou neiz, et estoit un poc declinans a la destre partie; et estoit li saiette toute reponue Je fui apelez a la cure aprés ceu qu’elle fut cheue III jors.	And one arrowed the king in the home of the princes, having been pierced through both eyes and leaning slightly to the right side; the arrow was entirely inserted. I was summoned for treatment after it was shot for three days.
Si trovai la plaie mult estroite.	I found the wound very tight.
Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I tried with all my subtle skill, and did not feel it; and there was a burn and pain under his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was due to the tip of the arrow. I placed a healing and digestive plaster on his ear because his ears were not inflamed; and I saw the arrow in the ear.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I placed the plaster on for several days and treated the wound immediately, so that the patient would endure this long duration, until they felt the arrow within their nose; and I told him this.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I applied corrosive aqua regia medicine to the wound for several days until it was opened, then tried it and felt the tip of the arrow moving toward my hand. After that, I placed the wound opening with this medicine, as long as the head of the arrow became visibly apparent; and passed through well in about four months, and then closed the wound so tightly that I could close the forceps firmly on either side, but it didn't come out; therefore, I continued to refine and engineer ways using tools until I took hold of the arrow with properly made forceps, as described at the end of this chapter, throughout the process, and left the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And they judge that the nasal cartilage cannot be restored: I will restore it then, and after sealing the wound, made the patient fully well.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Or this is what I told you about the quality of extracting arrows, so please apply your treatment on what I do not mention here because books cannot comprehend everything; but wise masters compare well on even a small number of things, and when something is present or lacking, they find new work and new tools, in anticipation of and due to the occurrences that happen within this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I state that arrows penetrate the limbs through two manners: either by the front where they enter or from another side; and when an arrow penetrates or enters from the front, it goes inside the flesh, and no longer pierces any time now.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if it doesn't jump now, let it stay until the body is decayed internally, and until its exit is free; also if it's stuck in bone, and can't escape, let it remain like that for some days, and remove it every day; and then it jumps, and if it doesn't jump, penetrate internally through all thin flesh, as long as the intestines are widened there, and then extract it.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if an arrow is stuck in the skull bone, and reaches up to one of the brain's cavities, or any other situation that I've mentioned for the patient: do not remove it immediately, but let it be until it stops moving after a few days. For when the arrow penetrates so far, this is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is only stuck in the bone and doesn't reach further than the sinus, and remains within the patient for any number of days without causing harm, then use a tool to remove it.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is only deeply embedded and cannot come out, if you administer hot baths internally, as I told you; then treat the wound until it heals.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is returned to its place within the body such that you cannot see it, then look all over; and if you feel it, try with any available tool; and if by constriction of the wound or depth of the arrow, and there's no bone, nerve or vein, cut as much as possible when the wound is large; pull out the arrow if you can, and if there are holes in the arrow where it holds, remove the flesh that has stuck from two parts, then break or bend the ears of the arrow as long as you can pull it; do so carefully not to break the arrow but pull it out more roughly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot remove it in one go, when the shaft is already deep into your arm, then proceed with its removal, because the extraction is painful.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the bleeding makes you contrary, then apply what we have said about treatment in our chapter; and guard against cutting near nerves and veins, and position as you can move to pull out the arrow without danger, quickly or slowly, firmly or gently; and place the patient according to the shape they were at when the arrow hit them, for this is the greatest aid that it should be like this, and if you cannot do so, then place them according to what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from elsewhere, or if there is any defect in it, or the skin is swollen at the spot so you can see or feel it oddly: cut therefore up high, as long as the forceps can take hold, and then pull: if it jumps now.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, rotate your hand around, until it enters into the bone, and widen the bone, then pull it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot come out, let it stay there for now, and then start extracting again as long as it comes out; and if the arrow is stuck in her, pull out the whole shaft. And if she farted, and you see how to administer forceps, if you need to use a tool with a pointed end, so that the tip of the arrow enters into the tool's hair; and then force it, and if the arrow is caught by its point, then pull out the tool at its point entering end, to facilitate extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if an arrow has pierced you, then it is necessary for you to hold all the flesh around where I have entered, if possible, and then treat the wound as seems fit.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if an arrow pierces the head or chest or stomach or bladder or ribs and it is close by, and you can hold up, then it is necessary to hold; and be careful not to cover the vein or nerve. Then extract it, and then treat the wound if needed; and heal until it is healed, and treat as long as she/he is well.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The shape of the forceps used for arrows resembles that of an eagle's beak, and here is its form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are of many kinds: large, medium-sized, and small, according to the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The shape at the arrow's tip is also like the feathers of a bird, to puncture at the point of the arrow, as this is its shape:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	the shape for pressing and gripping is like this:
des voinnes dou cors communes	of the veins of the common body
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	There are XXXI veins from which we bleed, of which there are XVI, namely: Two small arteries that are behind the ears, which are called "herbech"; and two arteries that are in two visible temples; and two veins that are in two eyelids of two eyes, which are called "aspires"; and the vein that is inside the forehead; and the vein that is at the nose's head; and the two jugulars that are in the neck; and the two veins that are above the mouth in the lips, and these are the veins that are called "augeherich"; and two veins that are under the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins that we commonly heal are: in each arm; one is the cephalic vein, and it is near the left rib, and they call it among laypeople "vein of the head"; and the middle one is called 'fascia', and it is composed of the cephalic vein and the basilic vein, and they call it among laypeople "vein of the heart"; and the basilic vein so is near the right rib, and they call it among laypeople "vein of the stomach", and it's above the clavicle, and this is the one that we heal, which opens clearly on the chest.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	The salvation vessel is the vein that's located between the thumb and the ring finger, and it has two courses; and in the leg and at the feet there are three veins: one of which lies along the curve of the chest near the left rib, and the second 'sophene' which is at the ankle near the right rib; and the vein that's called 'nurse', which is at the ankle on the other side. And in the other leg are three veins under these.

It has an opening through the center approximately a quarter along, as if to pierce a needle, like one from a spider, so that when it is placed on the body part it does not cause pain to the patient; and there's an opening at the center for an arachnid or iron thread across the middle, to insert a candle wick into. The size should be large and small depending on the diseases and condition of those using them; for children's suckers are different from adults', and slender ones differ from fatty ones.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And we should thus apply this suction cup to the body: take the wick or the thread of wax or linen, and insert it through the center of the suction cup, such that the light is at the bottom of the suction cup so it does not burn the patient; then place it on the body part, and your fingers either over the protrusion as we said, so that when desired, if the vapor goes inside, remove the suction cup; and take hold of the thread or wax in the same way, and repeat often, should you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	In the suction method therefore, which is administered in pleurisy disease, during all stages of fever, there is neither a tube nor a hole and it is not administered with force until it's full of water. And it is placed solely on the member; and this is how it should be done:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	Without tubes are administered only in members where one cannot put suction cups due to their small size, such as lips and gums, and similar parts; and in their unclothed areas of flesh, like elbows or knees, and other similar areas; and the quality of using them is that when you find without tubes that are in mild water without impurities, you take them. And you put one in mild water until they become accustomed, and have nothing in their stomachs; and then cleanse with a vein and suction cup treatment, then rub the member so it turns red, and place the tubes on it; and when they are full, and excrete, if it's an area where one can put a suction cup, you place it there because this works quite well.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If not this way, raise the arm with hot water very carefully, then cold water and mix them well. And then apply ointment. If the arm heals too soon after removing the stitches, moisten it with linen in cold water and place it on top until the wounds are healed; and if there are many wounds, put powdered vitriol or gall and similar things on them until they are healed; or you may put half a peeled bean under the arm, leave it there until the bean roasts on the arm, which will now stop bleeding. And if you need more of this method, prepare other stitches.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	And if the wounds do not heal properly, rub with fresh blood or insert a needle into them until the blood starts flowing and then place on top of it; as soon as they smell the blood, they will stop bleeding. And when you see that they are discharging, powder a little aloes and powdered meal, or ashes, onto them; they should heal now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	This begins the book on fractures
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	These chapters are often necessary in the art of medicine, and are for restoring breaks and recovery.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, good son, that these matters of this chapter which concern the inspection and treatment of wounds and ailments are not mentioned in any old books or read from letters; because of this reason, this knowledge has been estranged in our land as I never found anyone proficient. And I know nothing, having studied only through the knowledge contained within the ancient books that I've thoroughly reviewed, through experiments, and through life experience. I have described all these matters to you in this chapter accurately and summarized them clearly at the end. Moreover, I have illustrated the forms of instruments used in these treatments as done in the two chapters preceding this one.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	Therefore, it is necessary for us to outline or introduce the essence of this book and its chapters where wisdom places her understanding, remaining truthful, so that those who have been proven competent may know and learn this noble craft, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	I say that when any sort of injury, dislocation, twisting, or fever strikes anywhere in the body, you should attend to heal the patient on both sides immediately. If nothing seems amiss, such as weakness from coldness, young age, old age; if the affected part is too thickly clothed, too cool, or too cold; and consuming cold foods or drinks like cold joints (likely referring to raw meats), or eye or wild rabbit meat are not recommended. Do not drink wine, nor eat fatty meats, and do not fill up on heavy foods that can block blood flow in the veins until you are certain of no pus formation or spreading material inside the body; if only then should the patient be treated according to their first administration.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary to nourish the patient with foods that promote strong healing, or have a thick consistency, such as cooked wheat in water, and onions, and garlic, and liver, and kidneys, and cow stomachs, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar things.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For at any time of rupture it is necessary to let the parts move more quickly and soon the breaking.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that a bone broken in the old and the decrepit cannot be mended or joined well according to its nature due to the drying of the limbs, or those also which are too tender, such as bones of little children; but rather take care to reset on the broken bone the larger tendons which are attached and join the limb together, until it strengthens again as before. And do not finish his work hastily, for this is what befits him, nourishing with large meats, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that fractures can occur in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For breaking of the head is different from breaking at the ankle or leg, and I will tell you all methods of breaking in this chapter.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there are breaks that go to the tip, and others at the joints, such as the size of a feather for writing.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if it's a broken bone with an injury, or a break resulting in a small crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And each way has its tool and proper instrument in the restoration, according to what memory brings to his mind; and it is known that bone breakage can be identified by the twist of the limb, an obvious opening from below, and pressure on the hand; and when there's no twisting or rubbing involved, and no sensation of pain, if there's no breakage; but one may indeed experience twisting, or cracking, or small breakage.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	But do not move it with your hand yourself, but apply the remedies that follow, and then gently constrain it now.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the breakage that took place in the arm, and are its two parts separated, they should now put them on equal terms, as if you remove warts or varicose veins; and when warts come off, do not leave any day until the wart is calmed; then adjust it to make slight yet prudent movement, and know that healing after this is easier than healing in cases with pieces left behind; then hold it tight following these instructions.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are broken pieces in the bone, and it is split into two parts, whether it's hands or feet, or near your hand for smaller limbs, or divided by two strings, or one string with your hand; and place the limb according to its natural shape so that when the parts of the broken body have been removed, you can reset them in all directions using movements as light as you can manage, making sure there's no injury or pain from your actions. And adjust both ends of the bones properly into their best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And feel it well with your hand if you think it's not properly set: if it is set beautifully, and don't over-tighten, or apply pressure as those do who extract abscesses by their own method of contraction in the limb, as we have done many times.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the limbs are in place, severely restrain the patient so they do not move them, neither while awake nor while sleeping, neither while turning nor in any other way; ensure that the limbs are securely placed so they do not feel any pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	And when they do not feel any pain, it means they are not in the right position, and you should put them in such a position that they do not feel any pain. And make sure to place them correctly so that no deviation occurs when they are restored; and the quality of the broken limb is according to what I am telling you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	Know that limbs broken are varied by size and extent and shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	And there are small limbs like hands and arms and similar parts: one should wrap them with soft and fine linens. And for larger limbs such as thighs and legs: they need to be wrapped with a large firm bandage because the wider bands embrace the entire limb equally, from all sides without any gap. Then tie it in loops of light linen around three or four times according to the size of the member, making sure that your hand grips each band tightly. Once you are above the breakage point, apply less pressure so as not to move the break too much. And gradually soften the bandages little by little until a large part of the healthy limb is within reach. Then take another band and wrap it around the broken part from inside outwards. Then return slightly below the break and apply moderate pressure, neither too hard nor too soft, just as we have instructed in the first chapter above. After that place the light linen or bandages between each loop until they are all equal, then wrap everything with a belt above them, and finally, place your well-made staples there, provided there is no abscess or swelling.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is swelling or an abscess, put something soothing for the abscess in place, and which removes the swelling, and leaves it like that for a few days; then begin with your points, they should be half the width of a hair carefully inserted, or from the shaft used to make arrows, or of palm fronds, and align them according to this pattern:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	But it is necessary that the points that one places on the fracture be slightly larger and wider than the others; and should be as long as fitting to the size of each limb or greatness; then place them on the points just like you did in the first row, then fasten a small addition thread above, like in the first row on the breakage; more tightly is above, and less below; and it must be that the thread be medium sized, neither too big nor too small, and made of soft linen; for if the thread is large, as I want it from those who make their rows with twisted linen strings, and this is great error, because the row cannot be equal if it is too subtle, and it does not fit that there is less than two inches between each point.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patients are irritated by the shoulder blades after tightening during their recovery, place linen or raveled wool underneath them, so that they do not blister.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is accompanied by bruising, and the knees are broken, I will tell you the treatment below.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not right to constrain all broken limbs with bandages on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not suitable to use steel for this until after seven days or fourteen, or more according to your abscess situation; and here comes the manner of old plastering as restoration: you take flour that stands at the walls of the mill, mix it with enough egg, and make the concoction neither too thin nor too thick. Use this preparation and it is the common way for restoring fractures in various positions, equally so for men and children because there are no extremes of too hot or too cold involved.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana .x. З.; mirre et aloes, ana .v. З.; alechil .viiij. З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another way of plastering to restore fractures and dislocations and twists: take 3 parts each of garlic, dandelion leaves, rue, and asafetida, along with 9 parts gum arabic and myrrh; also include .v. (5) parts of aloes; add vinegar seven times its volume. Mix this powder well with plenty of egg whites; if the mixture is warm, use this plaster since it has a good composition and heals broken bones quickly, and is effective for many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plastering for torsion: take mastic and myrrh, each in quantity X III; take gum-resin and aloes, each in VIIII III; take carob six parts; take boric acid ten parts. Grind them well together, then mix with water or enough egg to make a paste, and apply it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method for the treatment of joints and bones that have moved out of their places, alleviating the pain arising from this, and trimming uses bone, and bone abrasion: take new wool, and cook it in oil and fat, then apply it to its place.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Wound plasters do not heal completely, but they are better for soothing abscesses and properly setting bones.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another method for plastering that heals broken bones: take dry fig leaves and terrestrial poplar leaves, grind them together, and make the plaster.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another method for plastering to restore bone fracture and to soothe the aftermath of an abscess.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take root of wild lettuce, chamomile, violet flowers, ground almonds, take the same amount from each; grind it together and mix with wine. If the limbs are inflamed, mix it with moist aniseed water or just water, then use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another method for faster plastering than the first, when an indurated abscess comes to heal on the member.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of vismalemel, and flaxseed, balsemum, melilot, and sansucius, and flowers of violets and chamomile, from all take a part; then grind and mix with salt water or sweetened water, or wine, according to the heat of the limb, and its rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ippocras instructs not to place anything on a broken limb for restoration except cerate made of wax and oil, and nothing else more, stating that it should be neither too soft nor too hard between two.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to Galen that one should place upon the broken member for restoration, dry things a bit heated, such as myrrh and aloe and incense and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another way to plaster for injury and pain: take mussels and goatskin grease or bird feathers, and vinegar, and oil equally, and grind them, and make a plaster from this mixture.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	Then remove the plaster a little later on, and be careful so that the patient does not feel any pain, nor is the bone of its place injured; if you do not remove it by hand day By day And when pain comes to the bone, or itchiness, without rest or swelling, then hasten, and remove it, and apply the plaster now; take a light cloth, and wet sponge, and dip them in water, and immerse the limb until the itch subsides and pain is relieved; then let the member rest for an hour, then place on dry wool, moistened with water or oil, and bind it to another nut, until you are sure of no more abscesses; and cool down the inflammation of the limb, and remove the pain, then restart the subtle application, a little plaster, and do not strain it as much as before; and refine gradually until it is healed.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you notice that pus has changed to a reddish color and pain along with swelling are subsiding, indicating healing throughout, then you will need to apply plaster and bandages again, proceeding in the same manner as before.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if there is no change in the limb that we have mentioned, or if it remains dislocated even after three to four or five or seven days; and leave it undisturbed for twenty days according to what we observe, until healing occurs, approaching the alignment of the bone; then you must hold back your restraint more than before, allowing the swelling's reduction, and focusing on aligning the flesh beneath; thus increase your strength, as I mentioned earlier; and if you notice that the limb dries faster than necessary, know that further dislocations are not possible; immerse it in hot water each time you reset it, every three days, cleanse a little of the wound; through this process remove the dislocations from the limb, correct swiftly what foolish practitioners do, causing the limb to remain bent: this is bad, and such practices lead to unnecessary harm, I have seen no other way than by patiently aligning and opening it directly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Through various methods of breaking up
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Many methods of fractures exist, and various forms. Their causes are distinct; for there are fractures produced by the impact of a sword, and the collarbone breaks all the bone up to the joint beneath it, just below the bone, as is done with an axe or staff. Thus, this method of fracture is termed 'hewing'.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces .ij. brisures grans ou petite.	Or the sword hits the bone from above without piercing it, and this type of fracture is called "absolute"; and both large and small injuries result from these two types of fractures.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is sequential impact, or a crack or collarbone fracture caused by stone, or on stone, or other similar conditions.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if it has fracture all the way to the membrane which is around the bone, or on top of the bone, and this wound can be large or small.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if there is a wound that has penetrated into the bone as fine as hair, and where the crack is small, thus this kind of fracture is called 'hairline'. And if the injury occurs due to striking with rock or falling, or from any other thing causing the piece of bone to be inserted within, and it lies in the bone like candle holders when they pierce into the wax candles; then the stone enters inside.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	This happens more often in individuals with moist bones, like those of children, and occurs through all these methods of fracture where many fragments are involved, such as in starfish injuries; and I will speak about that in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways of breakage by detachment from them, and the examination with forceps, and due to corrupted flesh that is present.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The appearance of hair is known by this: when one has exposed the bone and rubs it inwards, if there is an opening for black breakage.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the treatment of breakage, be vigilant against bad occurrences due to infection, and if you do not see any harmful adverse events, such as vomiting bile, loss of understanding, extension, fainting, ague fever, or if the eyes come out forcefully and turn red, and other similar signs in various dispositions, then cannot be healed without doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a serious emergency, yet still hope for salvation, start treatment immediately.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the birth comes to you first, and it is in winter, it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourteenth day after the month when you can.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it's in winter, you should hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the flesh around the bone becomes rotten, and accidents occur as we have said.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the breakage of the bone reaches as far as the membrane that covers the brain, then it must be that you cut the broken part like this: and you take hold of the head from the patient's body and uncover upon the bone in all ways that you can, and upon the appearance of the wound more surely than you can, and if the bleeding comes to reveal the bone, or pus appears, then do what is necessary there, and you fill the void with wet cloths in oil roset; and make the wound rest until the pus has subsided, and be sure of bleeding; then begin within the bone to remove, and this is done according to two ways of work: one way is that you cut at a narrow angle ahead, and this is the form:
Et puis i boute .i. autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then make another cut larger than the first one.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second method involves having several different cuts, some narrow and others wide, all with points made of iron. And work them gently to avoid injuring the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou .i. cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des .iij. manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is hard and protruding, it is necessary that you pierce through it internally, so that cuts are performed with needles, not straight cuts so they do not penetrate further than the bone under the testicle, and there should be a margin or a circle of about .i. (which could mean one inch) above the point that does not allow the point to pass beyond the bone; and you must have more than this, so that each comes in its place by the thickness of the bone, so that you have needles for all tests; and this is how the three kinds of needles are formed.
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes .i. tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality of piercing through the broken bone is such that you place one needle on the bone, and turn with your fingers until you know that the bone has been pierced. Then move another needle slightly after this point; then do so all around internally. Cut out the space between the parts of the bone where the punctures are, doing this more subtly and gently than possible, as we have said, until you bring the bone to your hand or any tool you might use such as forceps, tweezers; and make sure not to touch the brain or the spinal cord.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have cut through the bone and treated it, then it must be that you sharpen the scalpel which has remained from the bone to all other instruments resembling a file, but it must be more sturdy and more delicate than the other scalpel; and if there is nothing of small bones or any scales remaining, then gently scrape them off with the surgical tools; then cure the wound using ointments and treatments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And another way of working is this, as Galien stated, which is more careful; and the needle should be very strong, for it's his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first to expose a part of the bone, where the fracture opens and moves, so that once you have exposed that part, you will place under the tip of this lens-shaped incision, from which the form is as follows:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut from one side alone, and the limb is divided into two parts, so that you cut towards the bone; then with a small hammer above, such that you gently strike the entire bone, and be well cautious of the dust around it; if the skin is dry on the bone, you may lightly scrape it away because you remove the bone cleanly without harm and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone fracture doesn't go through to the membrane, and the bone is cut only above, and there are small pieces remaining, then you should clean up afterwards with a sharp blade, using various sizes so that each can be used most appropriately according to the manual instructions and the shape of the fracture.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you're using large剃刀, and then finer ones, and continue this process until it's done properly.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	For each of the finer hair trimming and subtle fractures, you must adjust your approach according to its direction; this is a matter that cannot be handled by someone who has dedicated their study to this craft.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the pus is revealed, it's necessary that you use linen drapes according to the size of the wound and soak them in oil rosette, then place them onto the wound; take another double layer of linen, soaked in wine and oil rosette, and place it above the first drape; do this more gently than possible, so as not to weigh down the pus, then administer another bandage from above, without exerting any force until only it touches the wound; leave it like that for one or two days, until the abscesses are no longer painful, then remove the bandage, and administer medicines such as roots of garlic, cornmeal, incense powder, and artemisia, among other things; from these create a powder and apply it to the wound, then administer further friendly medicines without causing pain; be careful that the wound is always clean, do not leave any ointment on it, nor allow any clotting on the skin under the brain, for when clots form there they spread and trouble the patient; because if you put something pungent on the pus, it will fester above.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Therefore, take care, should anything undesirable happen to the patient, as we have said, it leaves room for doubt without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fear does not come out only because of the medicine that we have put on it, that virtue exists, then you should take a part of honey, and three parts of roset oil, and one part in grease, and you apply this mixture to your skin; then you will treat as usual treatments, until it heals.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les .ij. parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont .ij. os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	Know that neither of the two parts below the nose are broken, or just one by itself, because they are two bones; and this lower one is cartilaginous, it does not break, nor can force cause it to be bent or twisted, then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two parts is broken, you should pinch your little finger or under your nose, and place that break inside your index finger, and out from the nostril, until the nose wakes up according to its natural shape; and do this lightly, making sure that the patient does not feel pain with your hand.

Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if the break is of two parts, redo this method, and try to restore it on the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or eighth day, when abscesses have subsided, then pinch under your nose with linen cloth pieces, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes .i. autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you apply another bandage from the other side, if the break is on that side as well; and make them large enough to cover the depressions around the nose.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And they say no restorer tells us to grease the tentacles with butter, and change each day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	It doesn't seem quite right to me, but it should be that they are greased during the preparation of a mixture of egg yolk and powder from flour; then let the tent be until the bone is hardened and the cartilage toughened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a .i. souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And always use goose feathers instead of tents, and if you have two raw eggs to cover them, and keep the bandage in place, then let the wound be exposed, letting air through it; do whatever you can see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en .i. poc de dyaquilon.	And if the pus comes out to the nose as you work on it, then put on a poultice or wet cotton in rose oil, or in a pinch of hydrazine.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the abscess is too deep to reach, then apply a poultice outside, made of poppy seed flour and incense powder, mixed with egg yolk; then place it on light bandages but do not tie them tightly around. de la routure de la mandibule	Regarding the rupture of the jawbone
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jawbone is ruptured internally and there's no wound outside,
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	It should be done as follows: If the breakage occurs in the right part of the jawbone,
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en .ij., si covient que tu aministres extension de .ij. pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if there's a breakage in both halves of the mandible,
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus .i. drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.
